Not just about life, but also about what's coming up next..what</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5515527424450722470" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418865295i/12925951._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="202" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>God, The cover is so attractive, yet deceiving..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409059738ra/10928140.gif" width="400" height="616" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's not Horror, not fast thriller and not That creepy..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418679958i/12868879.jpg" width="401" height="242" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418690198ra/12870383.gif" width="400" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Mostly it's about coming of age, Nostalgia..It's about Life..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418832967i/12917017.png" width="399" height="272" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Life; Movies &amp; "Paperbacks", Sex &amp; Drugs..And TOO MUCH Rock &amp; Roll..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418832967i/12917018.jpg" width="400" height="312" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418836286i/12917963.jpg" width="400" height="194" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's about a Shadow with no light..getting darker &amp; darker..till you <i>lose faith</i> that there's any light..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418690988i/12870426.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418691474i/12870474.jpg" width="400" height="143" alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And the only light you'll see here..is the Thunderous Lightnings.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418693933i/12870797._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="260" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yeah,it's also about losing faith. Not just about life, but also about what's coming up next..what's Death and what's beyond..<br>And it's about secret power..Electricity..lighting bolts..and Volts..</b><blockquote>"That is Not Dead which can Eternal Lie,<b> and with Strange Aeons Even Death may die"</b>
</blockquote><b>H.P. Lovecraft<br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401805535i/9850701._SX540_.jpg" width="399" height="225" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418689959i/12870360.jpg" width="400" height="55" alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*************************************<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418837654i/12918514.png" width="378" height="166" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's it...I can't spoil it to you, It was really great "living" with Jamie Morton for over 50 years...</b>"it's been 9 days for me but really seemed like years"<b><br><br>I really liked it..It's my first read for Mr. King and I know it's late but late better than never..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418840253i/12919220.jpg" width="400" height="96" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*************************************<br>The Story and the Characters<br>-----------------------------<br><br>A wonderful drawing of family life in the 60s...the early life of Jamie Morton, the tragedy of it too was very touching.<br> The coming of age..the sweet Nostalgia..and family reunions..<br> And I loved Reverend Charlie's character development, and basically all of them...<br> Mr. King really gave all his characters real life and real soul..<br>Even the setting, was so real, I told you I was "living" the novel..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418834944i/12917560._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="367" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I didn't like the Rock and Roll parts </b>-which was a bit too much-<b> since I'm not a big fan,but clearly Mr. King is..<br> but was okay to fast read these parts, also the sex and affairs which wasn't bad, just over talked about at some moments specially by the late chapters </b>-with the parts when Jamie and his partner tracking the revival's healed patients, I loved that parts was so creepy and thriller but slowed by his and her affair-.<br><b><br>It's also was hard to follow at some parts where was 'Too Much Capital Letter In The Beginning Of Each Word' that's refers always to names of musicians , local towns, roads , songs or whatever that requires you'd be so American and so into Rock and Roll. <br><br>On the other hand, I loved the many movies references and techniques specially at the beginning when the narrator showing how our lives similar to movies..I always believe that myself..<br> </b><blockquote>“But who is screenwriting our lives? Fate or coincidence?<br> I want to believe it’s the latter. I want that with all my heart and soul.<br> When I think of Charles Jacobs —my fifth business, my change agent, my nemesis— I can’t bear to believe his presence in my life had anything to do with fate. It would mean that all these terrible things—these horrors—were meant to happen. <br>If that is so, then there is no such thing as light, and our belief in it is a foolish illusion. If that is so, we live in darkness like animals in a burrow, or ants deep in their hill. And not alone.”</blockquote><b><br>And one more thing...Atheism...<br><br> May be it wasn't about Horror Carnivals as I've presumed before..<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418676943i/12868265._SX540_.jpg" width="401" height="298" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It wasn't "Joyful" as it may seem..It gets darker and darker..till you might lose faith in any joy..even light..as if it's the notorious "God Delusion" disguised into a novel..<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418693933i/12870796._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="317" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Terrible Sermon in the beginning of the Novel was "shocking" actually ...yet I can't deny It have some even little reason in it..</b><br><blockquote>“people always want a reason for the bad things in life. Sometimes there ain’t one.”</blockquote><br>And the irony here that I witness some terrible things too ,one very recent , just the day before I complete this review "16th Dec.2014 " A terrible accident to a dear friend's mother and granny Sunday morning while they were heading to Church ,to attend a funeral , lead to a death , and a serious injuries to the mother !!! <br><b>It's really dark novel , it was really a bit like some lives, that turn darker and darker as it moves on..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418837654i/12918514.png" width="378" height="166" alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The Revival part was haunting, The Cures...The Aftereffects, the seceret electricity...The Something that Happened...</b><br><blockquote>“Then they all began to sing. The tune was “Happy Birthday,” but the lyrics had changed. <br>“Something happened . . . TO YOU! Something happened . . . TO YOU! Something happened, dear Jamie, something happened TO YOU!” <br>That was when I began to scream.” </blockquote><br><b>It was slow </b>as I told you more like life and drama story <b> until the second half..When That Thing that Happened...and getting more dark..you'll never know may be till the last few lines why at the first page Jamie told us he hates Rev. Charlie.. was that because of the "Terrible Sermon"?<br>Well, I will let you discover yourself..<br></b><blockquote>“God isn’t as important to people now,” my mother said one day after a particularly disappointing turnout. “A day will come when they’ll be sorry for that.”</blockquote><br><b><br>I don't know why I felt it's really dark and for some reason,that there's no "Clear" point for me by the end which "team" Mr. King is -I'm sure he's not that dark- but I guess I will think about the ending for long..<br>I will read more H.P Lovecraft..and the other 10 authors this book dedicated for...</b><br><blockquote>“This is how we bring about our own damnation, you know-by ignoring the voice that begs us to stop. To stop while there's still time.”</blockquote><b><br>May be I didn't even know for sure what's That Thing that Happened ..<br>And I almost rate it 3...And still loved it, and if I go back in time would read it again...</b>But since that recent accident I mention yesterday..I rate it 4..and appreciate it a bit more..<b>And Sure I'll read more for The King of Horror.. Stephen King.</b><br><blockquote>“Life is a wheel, and it always comes back around to where it started.” </blockquote><b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418865295i/12925951._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="202" alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>From 6 Dec.2014<br>To 14 Dec. 2014<br><br></b><br><br>So....The First "Presume" is here "The Old Pre-review<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><b>God, That cover is so exciting one...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409059738ra/10928140.gif" width="400" height="616" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>I always love the theme of Horror Carnavals, Abandoned parks ,since some 80s and 90s Horror movies,and of course Goosebumps<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409050805i/10926720._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="581" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>And that's why I bought this year,to read later The Night Circus<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409137062i/10938277._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="609" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>And 'Revival' perhaps will be my first read for Mr. King, The Master of Horror,The most active writer with 4 BIG novels in 2 years, <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409137145i/10938281._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="640" alt="01" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Joyland one of those 4,successful 4,and also with my favorite theme,so it may be my next, after Mr. Mercedes <br><br>Can't wait to start my first long waited read for Mr. King<br></b><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>28 June 2014<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Annemarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie"><img alt="Annemarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593255949p2/27544490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3163320554?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annemarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annemarie" href="/user/show/27544490-annemarie">Annemarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783453438484" href="/book/show/31557142-revival">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27544490-annemarie?shelf=read-in-german">read-in-german</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3163320554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2815688378622960616">You shouldn't go into this book thinking is going to be super scary. It's more of a coming-of-age story. These are my favourite kind of books, I love reading about characters getting older and finding out what things and situations shape them and influence their life. <br/>So for me, this book was a wonderful little treat for in-between! It wasn't the most exciting or special book, and I definitely wouldn't recommend it to someone who hasn't read King before, but for an already established fan - this</span>
  <span id="freeText2815688378622960616" style="display:none">You shouldn't go into this book thinking is going to be super scary. It's more of a coming-of-age story. These are my favourite kind of books, I love reading about characters getting older and finding out what things and situations shape them and influence their life. <br />So for me, this book was a wonderful little treat for in-between! It wasn't the most exciting or special book, and I definitely wouldn't recommend it to someone who hasn't read King before, but for an already established fan - this is wonderful. I definitely liked it more than I expected.<br />However, it's also a book where I don't have a lot of things to say. I had a nice reading experience, but I know the story won't stick in my mind for very long. But that's not necessarily a bad thing! After all, not every book needs to be over the top amazing. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1104280454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1104280454" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1104280454?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/19196719-revival">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1104280454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4508514306707803408">The dust jacket of <i>Revival</i> promised a a contemporary Gothic novel in the <i>"great American tradition of Frank Norris, Nathaniel Hawthorne, and Edgar Allan Poe</i>, which would span five decades and contain <i>the most terrifying conclusion Stephen King has ever written</i>. Stephen King himself said that the book is <i>too scary"</i>, and that he doesn't want to think about it anymore, calling it <i>"a nasty, dark piece of work."</i>. This is his second book to be released this year, after the disappointing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966923078?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mr. Mercedes</a>. </span>
  <span id="freeText4508514306707803408" style="display:none">The dust jacket of <i>Revival</i> promised a a contemporary Gothic novel in the <i>"great American tradition of Frank Norris, Nathaniel Hawthorne, and Edgar Allan Poe</i>, which would span five decades and contain <i>the most terrifying conclusion Stephen King has ever written</i>. Stephen King himself said that the book is <i>too scary"</i>, and that he doesn't want to think about it anymore, calling it <i>"a nasty, dark piece of work."</i>. This is his second book to be released this year, after the disappointing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966923078?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Mercedes</a>. In comparison, <i>Revival</i> fares better - but that was a low point of comparison to begin with.<br /><br />Readers expecting a Gothic novel are bound to be disappointed, as much of the book is typical King fare. Although the structure at first looks like a homage to the form - the protagonist relating the horrors that he has already experienced in recollection, short summaries below each chapter - it soon lapses into familiar territory.<br /><br /><i>Revival</i> begins in the setting of so many of Stephen King novels, the ubiquitous small town in New England, and is narrated by Jamie Morton - a local boy who is the first to meet the town's new pastor, Charles Jacobs. Jacobs has just moved in with his wife and son, and quickly proves popular with the community , filling up the town church; he is also deeply passionate about electricity, which he describes to the church youth as a<i>"one of God's doorways to the infinite"</i>. Jacob's good fortune doesn't last long - after a horrible accident strikes his family, he gives his last sermon - in passion he denounces and ridicules religious belief and curses God with anger and fury. It's obvious that his career as a local preacher is over, and Jacobs soon leaves town.<br /><br />Jamie Morton grows up, and discovers his talent and passion for the guitar - he first joins a band in his school, and soon begins to perform professionally and tour with various bands, getting lost in drugs. This is my main problem with <i>Revival</i> - we've been here before; drug addiction is a running theme in many of King's novels, and main protagonists of books such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11588.The_Shining__The_Shining__1_" title="The Shining (The Shining #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shining</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78615336?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Tommyknockers</a> openly struggle with it. This isn't a surprise, as Stephen King himself was addicted to both drugs and alcohol during the 1980's - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10614.Misery" title="Misery by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Misery</a> is probably the clearest metaphor of addiction, with Annie Wilkes's deadly addiction to Paul Sheldon directly mirroring King's own destructive addiction to cocaine; his first "sober" novel is also about addiction though of a different kind, tellingly titled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107291.Needful_Things" title="Needful Things by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Needful Things</a>.<br /><br />The second main problem that I had with <i>Revival</i> is the lack of promised Gothic and pure horror. Approximately 3/4 of content is focused on Jamie's life - from his growing up in a small town and his relationship with his family, his first love and passion for music, and his downward spiral. King fans will delight in picking small references to his universe - the cities of Castle Rock and Jerusalem's Lot, Gunslingers, Roses and the number 19 among others - but I would argue that there's little of Edgar Allan Poe or Nathaniel Hawthorne to be found here. I was reminded of last year's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729038656?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Doctor Sleep</a>, where the main character was an alcoholic who also struggled with addiction and recovery. <br /><br />Luckily for us, Jamie's and Jacob's life intertwine throughout the book - Jamie meets his old friend at a carnival fair, where the reverend is creating "portraits in electricity". The meeting will have a drastic impact on Jamie, who will come to believe that Jacob's faith in electricity might not be entirely misguided. When Jamie and Jacobs will meet again, the pastor will reinvent himself as a faith healer in <i>The First Church of Electricity</i>, and although Jacobs's performances don't seem to be that different from other faith healers, Jamie will nonetheless suspect that there's something deeply troubling about them.<br /><br />The last quarter of the novel is the best of all, and this is the part of the book where - finally - the Gothic horror comes to life, and develops into something much greater. Although the theme of electricity brings to mind Mary Shelley's classic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18490.Frankenstein" title="Frankenstein by Mary Shelley" rel="nofollow noopener">Frankenstein</a>, the book owes a much larger debt to Arthur Machen's classic horror novella <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/564325981?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great God Pan</a>, and the writings of H.P. Lovecraft (whose classic quote ...even death may die" is the book's epigraph, and signifies things to come). The novel is dedicated to both writers (among others), but Machen is singled out as is <i>The Great God Pan</i>, which King says has haunted him "all his life". Still, I can't help but think that the impact of the ending was significantly diminished with the long buildup, which felt largely separate from it and non-horrific. It feels weird to write it about a tribute to the classics of cosmic horror, but I think that it was a case of the proverbial too little, to late.<br /> <br />I was also disappointed in the ending for another reason: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Claire, Jamie's beloved sister, was barely referenced after her tragic death; I almost expected her to make a reappearance at the end - Jacobs could have used her soul as a bargaining tool to get Jamie to help him. If Claire returned at the end, and was ultimately damned to eternal suffering because of Jamie's actions in helping Jacobs I think that the novel would have been much more dark and had a greater impact; hitting the reader - through Jamie's love for Claire - right in the gut; but it didn't, and that was very disappointing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />My hopes for <i>Revival</i> were high; I expected it to revive, if you'll pardon the pun, the classic horror that was promised to us. I expected a rich, atmospheric horror, in tradition of Stephen King's own <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">'Salem's Lot</a> or its great short story predecessor, <i>Jerusalem's Lot</i>, itself a tribute to Lovecraft's <i>Rats in the Walls</i>. This time the inspiration was too transparent, and in its ending sections <i>Revival</i> read as a homage to both Lovecraft and Machen - while I really wanted it to succeed and terrify on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4508514306707803408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_960159406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/960159406" />
    <a title="Ruth Turner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner"><img alt="Ruth Turner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435387851p2/17861817.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/960159406?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth Turner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth Turner" href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner">Ruth Turner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781476770406" href="/book/show/20926342-revival">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17861817-ruth-turner?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer960159406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13451225379519386580"><br/><br/>If someone had sat me down, told me they were going to read to me, and asked me to guess the author, the only reason I would have guessed correctly were the mentions of Castle Rock, Jerusalem’s Lot and Joyland. Otherwise I wouldn’t have had a clue.<br/><br/>There’s something missing in this dark story, and it’s a connection to the characters. It’s one thing I love about King, his ability to breathe life into the wonderful characters that people his books. But this one left me flat.<br/><br/>It’s not unusual for me </span>
  <span id="freeText13451225379519386580" style="display:none"><br /><br />If someone had sat me down, told me they were going to read to me, and asked me to guess the author, the only reason I would have guessed correctly were the mentions of Castle Rock, Jerusalem’s Lot and Joyland. Otherwise I wouldn’t have had a clue.<br /><br />There’s something missing in this dark story, and it’s a connection to the characters. It’s one thing I love about King, his ability to breathe life into the wonderful characters that people his books. But this one left me flat.<br /><br />It’s not unusual for me to read a book a day, especially when it’s a great story. But I’d only just made the halfway mark by day 3, and had begun to think I wouldn’t be able to finish it.<br /><br />It did pick up somewhat in the second half, but when I reached the climax of the story I was really disappointed. Seriously? That’s it??<br /><br />The book is exceptionally well written, which is no surprise, as Stephen King is an exceptional writer, and a master storyteller, but to me this was only just an ok read.<br /><br />At one point in the story Jamie is asked if he wants to go on stage and play guitar. He declines because…“skills fade as the years stack up” and I believe this to be true, and not only for Jamie. I think, with King, this is perhaps the reason why his later books don’t work for me. It’s a depressing thought that I may have read the best that’s in him. <br /><br />I enjoyed the early chapters and the Aftereffects, but the rest, not so much.<br /><br />And scary? No, not at all. King has scared the bejeezus out of me with much better nasties than Charlie Jacobs.<br /><br />***<br /><br />Audio Trailer - Narrated by David Morse: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://stephenking.com/promo/revival/#audio-trailer">http://stephenking.com/promo/revival/...</a><br /><br />Excerpt from chapter 6. Audio also.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.rollingstone.com/culture/features/stephen-king-exclusive-read-an-excerpt-from-new-book-revival-20141027?page=3">http://www.rollingstone.com/culture/f...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13451225379519386580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1431525939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431525939" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431525939?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1431525939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12439698478190803699">In 1962, while out playing in his yard, 6-year old, Jamie Morton, had a shadow fall upon him. He looked up to a statuesque man in church garb hovering over him.<br/><br/>The man introduces himself as Charles Jacobs, he's the new reverend, just arrived to town.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602638192ra/30234619.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jacobs, the Rev, is young, vibrant and successful at filling pews; breathing life back into the somewhat stale local church.<br/><br/>He also develops strong relationships with a lot of the young people, Jamie included, who actually is a favorite of sorts for </span>
  <span id="freeText12439698478190803699" style="display:none">In 1962, while out playing in his yard, 6-year old, Jamie Morton, had a shadow fall upon him. He looked up to a statuesque man in church garb hovering over him.<br><br>The man introduces himself as Charles Jacobs, he's the new reverend, just arrived to town.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602638192ra/30234619.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jacobs, the Rev, is young, vibrant and successful at filling pews; breathing life back into the somewhat stale local church.<br><br>He also develops strong relationships with a lot of the young people, Jamie included, who actually is a favorite of sorts for Jacobs.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551623374ra/27147883.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After tragedy strikes, Jacobs is prompted to move on. That's not the last time Jamie will come across him however; not by a long shot.<br><br>From there the narrative progresses with a classic coming-of-age feel and ultimately, ends up spanning five decades.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602638192ra/30234620.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We follow Jamie as he discovers his gift for music, finds first love, moves from home, struggles with addiction and encounters Jacobs again and again.<br><br>Jacobs is the shadow that falls over his entire life.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602638192ra/30234621.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I didn't come up with that. That's from the book, but definitely captures Jacobs presence in this story.<br><br>I loved the way King built this one up and progressed the narrative. As Jamie begins to realize the depths to which Jacobs has gone with his electrical obsession, and subsequent pursuit of its potential healing powers, the intensity continues to grow and grow and grow.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592594311ra/29674968.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The interactions between Jamie and Jacobs begin to feel more dangerous every time they meet.<br><br>Jacobs electrical work and experiments were so interesting, but most interesting of all to me, were his healings. The revival-tent displays of power. It had a real mad scientist energy that had me more charged than Frankenstein's monster.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1601431470ra/30170224.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Revival</i> is a stunning example of King's status as master storyteller.<br><br>From beginning to end, I was entranced. There is so much substance to be found within these pages; so many lines I wish I could recall at will. It's exceptional. I feel like I will carry this story with me for a long time to come.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445399579ra/16644259.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending is horrifying. Emotionally, philosophically, theologically; there's a lot to unpack.<br><br>We're talking full blown existential crisis upon reading the last 40-or so pages. I would love to read this again and annotate it. I definitely think it is worthy of that care.<br><br>Thank you to all my Constant Reader friends who finally pushed me to pick this one up. Loved it, loved it, loved it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602638192ra/30234622.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12439698478190803699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1737738545?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Corner" href="/user/show/46088881-reading-corner">Reading Corner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1737738545" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7472226923425859844"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This book is so underwhelming and over hyped.I've only read two other King books but after reading this,my opinion of the other two has completely gone up.I found most of <b>Revival</b> incredibly boring and tedious to get through.There's no real build up in this book like King has in his other books,the atmosphere never felt tense and there was no real suspense,until maybe the end.<br/><br/>I thought the story was really boring,until the end when everything adds up but even that ending couldn't save th</span>
  <span id="freeText7472226923425859844" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />This book is so underwhelming and over hyped.I've only read two other King books but after reading this,my opinion of the other two has completely gone up.I found most of <b>Revival</b> incredibly boring and tedious to get through.There's no real build up in this book like King has in his other books,the atmosphere never felt tense and there was no real suspense,until maybe the end.<br /><br />I thought the story was really boring,until the end when everything adds up but even that ending couldn't save this book.The story is dragged out and could easily cut 100 pages.I didn't care about any of the characters as I didn't think any were particularly interesting.Would I recommend this book?<b>No</b>.I recommend trying King's others books and give this one a miss.</span>

<div id="review_1110947084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1110947084" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1110947084?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1110947084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16351218283942543983"><b>
  <i>"People always want a reason for the bad things in life. Sometimes there ain't one."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Almost everyone assured me that this is King's scariest, darkest, and creepiest novel to date. I don't completely disagree with the numerous acclaims, but I am considering this novel as heavily flawed. The plot was immersing, but only to a certain extent. I now understand why some people warned me that this novel was a bit dragging in the middle. A lot of uninteresting things did happen in the middle, and it </span>
  <span id="freeText16351218283942543983" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"People always want a reason for the bad things in life. Sometimes there ain't one."</i>
</b><br /><br />Almost everyone assured me that this is King's scariest, darkest, and creepiest novel to date. I don't completely disagree with the numerous acclaims, but I am considering this novel as heavily flawed. The plot was immersing, but only to a certain extent. I now understand why some people warned me that this novel was a bit dragging in the middle. A lot of uninteresting things did happen in the middle, and it made the novel a bit dull. <br /><br />King never steps back from the line between sanity and insanity. This novel leaped beyond insanity, and I'm glad that it did. This is King's specialty, horror. I wanted to be scared to the point of being unable to sleep, but honestly I was only a bit creeped out of the last few chapters, and that was it. The plot was not completely forgettable, but it's not something new, for me. There is one novel that popped up in my mind while reading this, and that would be King's older novel, Pet Sematary. They both had a similar theme, plot, and ending. The difference would be that Pet Sematary was executed way better, in terms of plot and characters. I hate to compare, but the resemblance can't be overlooked. Pet Sematary will forever be one of my favorite novels, but sadly I can't say the same for Revival. <br /><br />This novel was not all bad though, and there are a lot of good things to say about it. The most prominent one would be the writing. You can never go wrong with King's writing. It will always be enthralling and would keep you reading till the end. It's not just the plot alone that does that, but the writing can have a huge effect on the reader's reading experience. King just knows what words to use, and how to properly construct an interesting sentence and paragraph. This is why I consider him to be a master story teller. He knows how to keep your attention.<br /><br />The characters were a mix of good and bad. Jamie was interesting and didn't seem to annoy me in any way. I mostly like King's main characters, and Jamie is not an exception. The rest of his family were also interesting, and that's why I enjoyed most of the first chapters. The antagonist on the other hand, Charles Jacobs, was annoying as hell. He wasn't consistent from beginning to end. It felt like I was reading a different character in the latter parts. I know it might be necessary for the plot development, but I didn't like the sudden change in attitude. It didn't result into development, but rather confusion. He also had a certain vibe that I didn't like. He was obviously fake from the beginning, so all throughout the novel he was just annoying me.<br /><br />The plot, like I said, was great. It had an interesting premise, and the conclusion was near satisfactory. If I haven't read Pet Sematary, I believe I wouldn't have predicted the ending. Less than halfway through the novel I already had a huge guess what the ending was going to be, and I'm disappointed that I was right. I like a good plot twist, something that would knock me out of my seat, but sadly this novel didn't do that to me. I know a lot of people who were caught off guard though, so maybe it's just me.<br /><br />There are a lot of quotable lines in the novel, but I would be robbing you from the experience if I added all of them in here.<br /><br />3.5/5 stars. Most of my friends loved this, but I've read better from King. I am considering this a really good horror/paranormal book, but not his best. If you're new to King then I'm quite positive that you'd be mesmerised by this novel. Highly recommended to horror aficionados and King fans. I know a lot of diehard King fans who still enjoyed this, so once again, it might just be me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16351218283942543983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1103385194" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103385194" />
    <a title="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh"><img alt="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532904571p2/7897213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103385194?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤" href="/user/show/7897213-andrea-ninja-bunneh">Andrea ❤Ninja Bunneh❤</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Old school bitches. </span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103385194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13818117823348378428"><a href='http://i.imgur.com/Phctlyd' title='' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415809696ra/11848832.gif' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Anyone, and I mean <b>anyone</b>, who thinks Uncle Stevie has lost some of his edge over the last few years shall now eat his/her words. Me being one of them. Now I know you're saying to yourself - <i>what the fuck, Andrea? You love Stephen King! You've been reading him for three decades practically! How dare you say such things! Have you lost your damn mind? </i><br/><br/>And I do. I adore King. He's the only author that I have followed religiously since pre-teendom. The only author that although some books don't </span>
  <span id="freeText13818117823348378428" style="display:none"><a href="http://i.imgur.com/Phctlyd" title="" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415809696ra/11848832.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Anyone, and I mean <b>anyone</b>, who thinks Uncle Stevie has lost some of his edge over the last few years shall now eat his/her words. Me being one of them. Now I know you're saying to yourself - <i>what the fuck, Andrea? You love Stephen King! You've been reading him for three decades practically! How dare you say such things! Have you lost your damn mind? </i><br><br>And I do. I adore King. He's the only author that I have followed religiously since pre-teendom. The only author that although some books don't resonate with me, I still know that the next one will be better. I just know it. But, I have missed the old school King over the years. The raw, disturbing, gut wrenching, on the edge of your seat <i>horror</i> that was delved out in King's darker days. <br><br><i>Revival</i> is old-school horror master King. I couldn't put it down. I wanted to throw an Uncle Stevie party and bake a cake in his likeness to celebrate. Although, saner minds prevailed and nixed that plan in the ass. <br><br>This is horror. The slow built up horror that clutches your brain in its claws and doesn't let you escape. The horror that when it ends, you're just left with this gut emptiness. On the edge of the emptiness sits a little bird who whispers <i>Holy balls, can that be real?</i><br><br>It's that same little bird who whispered to you when you were a kid that there's a monster hiding under your bed. The one that warned you about the basement and the closet. The one that told you clowns are not always good or funny and may have big teeth that want to eat you. The little bird that kind of faded away as you got older because you now had to take care of grown up responsibilities and stop being frightened of childish creepy things.<br><br>You grow and laugh at your childhood fears. Yet, you still always put the light on when you go into the basement or open the closet door. You still hesitate to put your foot on the floor when you need to get up in the middle of the night. You still have a subconscious aversion to clowns with their white painted on faces and fluffy orange hair. <br><br>You grow up and know that everything that little bird told you isn't real. I mean, it can't be. Right?<br><br><br>This book may remind you otherwise. <br><br><a href="http://i.imgur.com/MSAH9lQ" title="" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415810254ra/11848936.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Welcome back, Mr. King. I've missed you. <br><br><b>5 Ninja Bunnehs Wearing Gold Rings</b></span>

<div id="review_1016219648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1016219648" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016219648?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20942904-revival">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=all-hail-the-crimson-king">all-hail-the-crimson-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=scare-the-pants-off-ya">scare-the-pants-off-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016219648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4881435127063630302">I’m not sure that I have ever felt as conflicted about my feelings on a book by Stephen King as I do about Revival. I loved it. I hated it. It was ok. It was brilliant. It was a letdown. It was weird. It was something.<br/><br/>I was hooked right from the start. If there is one thing King is top-notch at- it’s creating a rich atmosphere about youth growing up in the good ole days. I think that is why <i>IT</i> will remain my all-time favorite book. There is nothing better than King writing about the 1950’s. I al</span>
  <span id="freeText4881435127063630302" style="display:none">I’m not sure that I have ever felt as conflicted about my feelings on a book by Stephen King as I do about Revival. I loved it. I hated it. It was ok. It was brilliant. It was a letdown. It was weird. It was something.<br /><br />I was hooked right from the start. If there is one thing King is top-notch at- it’s creating a rich atmosphere about youth growing up in the good ole days. I think that is why <i>IT</i> will remain my all-time favorite book. There is nothing better than King writing about the 1950’s. I already have an unnatural obsession with that particular decade so anytime there’s a book set in that time period it automatically tops my list. I realize we meet Jamie Morton in 1962 but once again, King manages to transport his readers back to that exact moment in time and it’s so believable you forget the world you live in. The events that take place in that first quarter or so of the book are just incredible. I loved every word.<br /><br />It’s when we flash forward to older, drug-addicted Jamie that King kind of lost me. I’m ok with character growth and I am definitely ok with characters spiraling down into a pit of addiction and self-destructive behavior. Here’s what I don’t like- getting a brief rundown of “Here’s how it was….here’s how it is now.” with nothing in the middle to get me there. I especially don’t like this when there’s repeated mention of what happened to Claire and then no further elaboration. I felt that was really a misused piece of information that was crucial to Jamie’s regression and damnit I wanted to read more about that! <br /><br />The same can be said for Mr. Charlie Jacobs. We understand that what happens to him, or rather to his family, is going to affect him greatly. I honestly would have loved to see more of his breakdown. I loved where King took Charlie as far as him turning into this crazed psychopath whose obsession completely takes over his life. That was brilliant! But once again, we touch on it, we hear whispers about it and then we jump ahead. Overall I found all of the time hopping to be rather choppy and poorly executed. King is so much better at crossing decades of time than he showed in Revival. It felt disconnected and somehow unrelated. The events merely spots on a timeline. <br /><br />Being the avid King reader that I am I did love finding the Easter eggs. I loved that Charles Daniel Jacobs is 19 letters long. I <b>really</b> enjoyed the electricity obsession that Charlie was so keen on proving. I loved what he wanted to do. I could see the madness in his eyes. (Aside: I totally picture Gus from Breaking Bad as Charles Jacobs in this. End of Aside). I found myself gripping my kindle waiting to see what was on the other side, what would happen when that bolt of lightning struck that pole. I was just as excited as Charlie, if not more so. <br /><br />I see a lot of people upset with what was on that other side. I, for one, wanted to damn the King to an eternity in Todash. It’s true. But not for the same reasons as other people. I know a lot of people are upset over the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Evil Ant Overlords <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but that didn’t bother me. After reading the Dark Tower I think I was prepared for something like this. The first line that came to mind was the one about our whole universe existing in a single blade of grass. The concept that size defeats all and that our minds are not capable of processing it. I wanted to damn Stephen King because the thought of death creates this paralyzing fear in me (a fear I don’t talk about often) and the picture he painted was not a promising one. All jokes aside, I texted my friend Jason and told him “I never even thought of that as an afterlife possibility”. And what I mean is that I am already terrified and King just sent me over the edge.<br /><br />Overall this book left me wanting more and wanting to see a shrink. There were aspects of it that I loved so deeply that I could almost literally feel my heart making room for them. Then there were parts that made me think “Is this really Stephen King writing this?!” So, I have rated this book 3 stars with a confused heart. I think I will revisit this one sooner than usual and reevaluate. I just can’t feel firm in my decision on rating this book at all. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4881435127063630302" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_878598210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878598210" />
    <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede"><img alt="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487436758p2/1379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/878598210?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789100142742" href="/book/show/23562384-v-ckelse">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer878598210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13437923569836407007">For a while, I actually thought that this would be the first book I would give five stars to in ages. But in the end, it just got four stars. Why? Because of the ending. I just didn't like it very much. It was very depressing and for some reason, it felt like a letdown. All I could think was: "Is that all, have I been reading all day for that kind of ending?" I would rather have had a more ambiguous ending to the story. Instead of just the bleak ending. (I need to read something cheerful after t</span>
  <span id="freeText13437923569836407007" style="display:none">For a while, I actually thought that this would be the first book I would give five stars to in ages. But in the end, it just got four stars. Why? Because of the ending. I just didn't like it very much. It was very depressing and for some reason, it felt like a letdown. All I could think was: "Is that all, have I been reading all day for that kind of ending?" I would rather have had a more ambiguous ending to the story. Instead of just the bleak ending. (I need to read something cheerful after this...) However, I'm sure there are people that will love the ending, and it was not a bad ending, but perhaps I'm just a gal that what some hope in the end...<br /><br />The rest of the book was great, I love Jamie and his family. I love watching him growing up, hell I would have loved reading a book about Jamie's life without Charles Jacobs. I know Jamie would have been a hell of a lot of happier without him in his life. Stephen King is a master telling tales, he has an uncanny ability to create interesting characters (both good and bad) and this book is one his greatest!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13437923569836407007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11776166140753689694">My review for this was somehow deleted -- so, yay for me! Regardless, this book wasn't amazing -- I still remember having to force myself to read it. So, I <i>am</i> tempted to lower the rating, because 3 stars seems pretty high. But, I won't.<br/><br/>I swear, the only reason I gave this 3 stars was because the guy I liked (years ago) had enjoyed this and I was <i>determined</i> to like it, too -- so we could have something to talk about. It's funny how a crush can make you like a book more than you actually would've.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2222699405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2222699405" />
    <a title="Jonathan Janz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4415785-jonathan-janz"><img alt="Jonathan Janz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518203259p2/4415785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2222699405?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Janz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Janz" href="/user/show/4415785-jonathan-janz">Jonathan Janz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222699405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17486674713890005367">In his best short fiction, Edgar Allan Poe achieved a "unity of effect." In tales like "The Tell-Tale Heart" and "Masque of the Red Death," the whole is greater than the sum of its parts. Each word, each turn of phrase flows toward a swirling vortex, a glowing, pulsing spire that pierces the steely thunderheads and rivets your gaze even as it threatens to lay waste to everything around it. <br/><br/>More on that later. <br/><br/>This unity of effect is difficult enough to create in a short piece of fiction. Thomas </span>
  <span id="freeText17486674713890005367" style="display:none">In his best short fiction, Edgar Allan Poe achieved a "unity of effect." In tales like "The Tell-Tale Heart" and "Masque of the Red Death," the whole is greater than the sum of its parts. Each word, each turn of phrase flows toward a swirling vortex, a glowing, pulsing spire that pierces the steely thunderheads and rivets your gaze even as it threatens to lay waste to everything around it. <br /><br />More on that later. <br /><br />This unity of effect is difficult enough to create in a short piece of fiction. Thomas Ligotti did it in "The Frolic," Richard Matheson in "Born of Man and Woman." <br /><br />The number of novels that have accomplished a unity of effect is even smaller. Shirley Jackson's THE HAUNTING OF HILL HOUSE is one; Cormac McCarthy's THE ROAD is another. After finishing REVIVAL last night, I'm ready to add another title to this sparse but jaw-dropping tradition. <br /><br />I wouldn't call REVIVAL my favorite Stephen King novel. In fact, it'd probably land somewhere in the six-to-ten range (after classics like 'SALEM'S LOT, THE STAND, and others). However, REVIVAL is better *written* than the aforementioned titles (with the caveat that no one but King could have written the others; when we’re talking about the master, we’re splitting hairs among some of the best pieces of horror fiction ever created; it’s like the difference between Da Vinci’s Last Supper and his Mona Lisa—they’re both extraordinary).<br /><br />But what blows my mind about REVIVAL is how “grooved” it is. Even though the narrative spans, what? Half a century? The feel of the book is one of fated inevitability. Even though what happens in the tale stems from the characters’ choices, the story feels like it couldn’t have gone any other way. Which brings me to the other facet of the book that still, nearly a day later, has my mind racing. <br /><br />A friend told me he felt as though King “really took the gloves off” for the novel’s climax, and that’s a great way to put it. I guess the story could have ended some other way, but it wouldn’t have captured the full breadth of the novel’s potential had King not followed the characters’ trajectories so faithfully. <br /><br />And herein lies an intersection between King’s theory about stories and Poe’s unity of effect. King believes that writers are archeologists, discovering tales like buried artifacts and exhuming them as faithfully and meticulously as possible. I imagine it’s how Poe must have felt when writing “The Black Cat.” Poe was able to exhume that twisted narrative from the depths of his imagination, and in doing so, he fully captured the story’s magnificence. Reading “The Black Cat” is like climbing into a coal cart and being thrust by a lunatic subterranean dweller down a rusty, perilous set of rails, and even if you survive the careening journey in body, by ride's end you've sacrificed a bit of your sanity. <br /><br />That’s how I felt reading REVIVAL. <br /><br />There’s one last thing I want to mention, and then I’ll give way to the master so you can experience this splendid, ghastly novel for yourself. It has to do with the awe-inspiring and dreadful hellscape I alluded to in the beginning of this review. <br /><br />By King’s own admission, this tale and several of his others (especially the glorious fever dream known as “N.”) owe a debt to Arthur Machen’s seminal story “The Great God Pan.” Machen’s story is one of the finest yarns ever written, and it continues to cast its spell on legions of modern readers and writers (Yours Truly included). But while Machen only intimates what lies beyond the veil, King tears the fabric wide open and allows the shrieking horror of what lurks there to scorch our retinas and destroy our minds. <br /><br />In other words, King *goes there,* and he drags us with him whether we're ready or not. <br /><br />Unity of effect. Narrative boldness. An indelible, poetic evocation of a place previously unimaginable. You’ll find all of these things and more in REVIVAL. <br /><br />Your mileage may vary, but for me, the master has never been better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17486674713890005367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14235349366553094228"><b>ReVolting Revival</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477441000ra/20952098.gif' width='300' height='197' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>"My mind raced<br/>And I thought what could I do (<i>Thunder</i>)<br/>And I knew<br/>There was no help, no help from you (<i>Thunder</i>)"<br/>AC/DC, "Thunderstruck," 1990<br/><br/>King's wizardry charges through Jamie Morton's ominous odyssey into the darkest forces of evil. The novel methodically intensifies a menace like the bass drum in the "2001 Space Odyssey" theme (from Strauss's <i>Also sprach Zarathustra</i>) as the Dickensian Jamie travels deeper and deeper into a supernatural storm with a defrocked Methodist minister </span>
  <span id="freeText14235349366553094228" style="display:none"><b>ReVolting Revival</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477441000ra/20952098.gif" width="300" height="197" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>"My mind raced<br>And I thought what could I do (<i>Thunder</i>)<br>And I knew<br>There was no help, no help from you (<i>Thunder</i>)"<br>AC/DC, "Thunderstruck," 1990<br><br>King's wizardry charges through Jamie Morton's ominous odyssey into the darkest forces of evil. The novel methodically intensifies a menace like the bass drum in the "2001 Space Odyssey" theme (from Strauss's <i>Also sprach Zarathustra</i>) as the Dickensian Jamie travels deeper and deeper into a supernatural storm with a defrocked Methodist minister (Charles Jacobs: J.C. backwards) hell-bent on revenge and corrupted by resentment against religion to the point of heresy, contempt and possibly insanity. Shades of Poe, Hawthorne and O'Connor via an electrified modern-day <i>Elmer Gantry</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467589040i/19607694._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="239" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I like this change of pace and find the story more terrifying because King slowly builds layer upon layer of evil to a crashing crescendo. While I don't consider it one of King's best, I do continue to appreciate his bottomless well of Lucifer-ous imagination.</span>

<div id="review_2834753536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2834753536" />
    <a title="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84916113-somebunny-reads-phoenix"><img alt="¸¸.•*¨*•♫♪SomeBunny Reads (Phoenix)•*¨*•♫♪" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600928258p2/84916113.jpg" /></a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2834753536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8424130369476252758"><i>That’s how you know you’re home, I think, no matter how far you’ve gone from it or how long you’ve been in some other place.   <span id="freeText8424130369476252758" style="display:none"><i>That’s how you know you’re home, I think, no matter how far you’ve gone from it or how long you’ve been in some other place. Home is where they want you to stay longer.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559063849ra/27584717.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I don't know how this Stephen King book escaped my radar back in 2014: I am the biggest King fan and I usually read everything he publishes. Unfortunately, I haven't been very lucky with the most recent books. This one, however, made me feel those <i>good ol' King</i> vibes all over again and oh am I glad I read it!<br><br>For starters, the book follows the life of the protagonist from his childhood to his adolescence to his last years; this is something I especially love in King's books because I think he excels in describing the evolution of a character during the years, creating a fully developed human being, absolutely interesting and unique, and totally realistic. This is not easy to do and, in my opinion, not many writers are good at it. I am especially in love with the way King describes adolescence and late teens: school, the first cigarette, the first sexual experiences, the passion... King never fails to make me emotional with the air of nostalgia and longing he communicates when describing high school years.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1559063849ra/27584716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The plot of this novel is not exactly unpredictable, and many clues throughout the book hint us to where the climax is headed, but the way King makes you wander all the time exactly <i>what</i> is going to happen, and <i>when</i>, manage to keep the suspense high through the book even though, as often in King's books, the story unfolds very slowly.<br><br>I loved this book as a novel, but this is a horror book and I should also review it as such. Unfortunately, the kind of horror this novel portrays, even though I appreciated its gothic and lovecraftian nature, isn't exactly substance of nightmares for me. Being scared is a very personal thing, and I think I just don't share this kind of fears. As I said though, I got very strong lovecraftian vibes (the creatures, the descriptions, but in particular the reference to an otherworldly colour) and - Lovecraft being one of my favourite authors of all time - this made me love the book even more. It just didn't exactly <i>scare</i> me, that's all. Overall, this is one of the best Stephen King book I read in a long time!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444505967ra/16510172.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8424130369476252758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer11065553780559089990">I'm just going to say this is the best King novel I have read in a long time.<br/>I wrote two different reviews (long and thoughtful, both) and lost internet signal before saving either one.<br/>Not happening again, folks.<br/>Buy this and dive in to a genuine treat. King is at his best. It starts out as a coming of age tale told in first person. The narrator, Jaime first meets Charles Jacobs as a six-year old and then their lives intersect over the next fifty plus years. Their fates are seemingly interlocked.</span>
  <span id="freeText11065553780559089990" style="display:none">I'm just going to say this is the best King novel I have read in a long time.<br />I wrote two different reviews (long and thoughtful, both) and lost internet signal before saving either one.<br />Not happening again, folks.<br />Buy this and dive in to a genuine treat. King is at his best. It starts out as a coming of age tale told in first person. The narrator, Jaime first meets Charles Jacobs as a six-year old and then their lives intersect over the next fifty plus years. Their fates are seemingly interlocked.<br />Bad things were bound to happen, but I didn't see that ending coming at all.<br />It's bleak, but in the best way.<br />Loved it!</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2mJtfrY5jUcm+CMWuoRBn6X9/Fj2PnybxaXGE+0XgYU3EAokFdEeDrWZJYlFpi05D5fsDHViJkWwLVZpeC/70w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gVjifcrN6NVb8aKb67vl9G/3Mh6/tfSwb6ULX/HpEapsKoUnaSV7nMiQpAQUmYlSxZ0iSjzprm4aLZslZNFr/A==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7560137064238090568">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText7560137064238090568" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7560137064238090568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
